152 BE IT ENACTED BY THE COUNCIL OF THE DISTRICT OF COLUMBIA, That this
153 act may be cited as the “Fiscal Year 2026 Budget Support Congressional Review Emergency Act
154 of 2025”.
155 TITLE I. GOVERNMENT DIRECTION AND SUPPORT
156 SUBTITLE A. FOIA CLARIFICATION
157 Sec. 1001. Short title.
158 This subtitle may be cited as the “Freedom of Information Clarification Congressional
159 Review Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
160 Sec. 1002. Section 204(a) of the Freedom of Information Act of 1976, effective March
161 29, 1977 (D.C. Law 1-96; D.C. Official Code § 2-534(a)), is amended as follows:
162 (a) Paragraph (20) is amended by striking the phrase “; and” and inserting a semicolon in
163 its place.
164 (b) Paragraph (21) is amended by striking the period and inserting a semicolon in its
165 place.
166 (c) New paragraphs (22) and (23) are added to read as follows:
167 “(22) Information or data provided by any court, federal agency, or federally
168 established agency to the Criminal Justice Coordinating Council, established by the Criminal
169 Justice Coordinating Council for the District of Columbia Establishment Act of 2001, effective
170 October 3, 2001 (D.C. Law 14-28; D.C. Official Code § 22-4231 et seq.);”
8

171 “(23) Information or data provided by any court, federal agency, or federally
172 established agency to the District of Columbia Sentencing Commission, established by the
173 Advisory Commission on Sentencing Establishment Act of 1998, effective October 16, 1998
174 (D.C. Law 12-167; D.C. Official Code § 3-101 et seq.); and”.
175 SUBTITLE B. CULTURAL AND COMMUNITY AFFAIRS
176 Sec. 1011. Short title.
177 This subtitle may be cited as the “Cultural and Community Affairs Congressional Review
178 Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
179 Sec. 1012. Cultural and community affairs grants.
180 (a) The Mayor may issue grants, in accordance with the requirements set forth in the
181 Grant Administration Act of 2013, effective December 24, 2013 (D.C. Law 20-61; D.C. Official
182 Code § 1-328.11 et seq.), to individuals and organizations that provide services to District
183 residents to support cultural affairs, community relations, and community partnerships.
184 (b) The Mayor shall provide centralized review and approval of grants issued pursuant to:
185 (1) Section 303(10) of the District of Columbia Latino Community Development
186 Act, effective September 29, 1976 (D.C. Law 1-86; D.C. Code § 2-1313(10));
187 (2) Section 3(c)(10) of the Office and Commission on African Affairs Act of
188 2006, effective June 8, 2006 (D.C Law 16-111; D.C. Official Code § 2-1392(c)(10));
189 (3) Section 3(b)(3) of the Office on African American Affairs Establishment Act
190 of 2017, effectively February 17, 2018 (D.C. Law 22-59; D.C. Official Code § 2-1398.02(b)(3));
9

191 (4) Section 304(c)(9) of the Office on Asian and Pacific Islander Affairs
192 Establishment Act of 2001, effective October 3, 2001 (D.C. Law 14-28; D.C. Official Code § 2-
193 1373(c)(9));
194 (5) Sections 4(b)(11), (11A), and (12) and 4a of the Office of Gay, Lesbian,
195 Bisexual, and Transgender Affairs Act of 2006, effective April 4, 2006 (D.C. Law 16-89; D.C.
196 Official Code §§ 2-1383(b)(11), (11A), and (12), and 2-1384);
197 (6) Section 3(b)(3) of the Office on Caribbean Affairs Establishment Act of 2020,
198 effective May 6, 2020 (D.C. Law 23-87; D.C Official Code § 3-1452(b)(3));
199 (7) Section 3(b)(2)(L) of the Office on Ex-Offender Affairs and Commission on
200 Re-entry and Ex-Offender Affairs Establishment Act of 2006, effective March 8, 2007 (D.C.
201 Law 16-243; D.C. Official Code § 24-1302(b)(2)(L)); and
202 (8) Section 704(6A) of the Office of Veterans Affairs Establishment Act of 2001,
203 effective October 3, 2001 (D.C. Law 14-28; D.C. Official Code § 49-1003(6A)).
204 Sec. 1013. Section 304(c)(8) of the Office on Asian and Pacific Islander Affairs
205 Establishment Act of 2001, effective October 3, 2001 (D.C. Law 14-28; D.C. Official Code § 2-
206 1373(c)(8)), is amended by striking the phrase “of the Office in accordance with an act of
207 Congress” and inserting the phrase “of the Office” in its place.
208 Sec. 1014. The Commission on Fathers, Men, and Boys Establishment Act of 2014,
209 effective February 26, 2015 (D.C. Law 20-155; D.C. Official Code § 3-731 et seq.), is repealed.

257 SUBTITLE C. SURPLUS PROPERTY FUND
258 Sec. 1021. Short title.
259 This subtitle may be cited as the “Surplus Property Sales Fund Congressional Review
260 Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
261 Sec. 1022. Section 805 of the Procurement Practices Reform Act of 2010, effective
262 October 22, 2015 (D.C. Law 21-36; D.C. Official Code § 2-358.05), is amended as follows:
263 (a) Subsection (c) is amended to read as follows:
264 “(c) Money in the Fund shall be used to pay the operational costs of OCP.”.
265 (b) Subsection (d) is amended to read as follows:
266 “(d) Any money remaining available in the Fund at the end of a fiscal year, as determined
267 by the Chief Financial Officer in the fiscal year-end close, shall be transferred to the unassigned
13

268 fund balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia as part of the fiscal year-end

270 SUBTITLE D. RECREATIONAL FACILITIES ASSESSMENT
271 Sec. 1031. Short title.
272 This subtitle may be cited as the “Recreational Facilities Assessment Congressional
273 Review Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
274 Sec. 1032. The Department of General Services Establishment Act of 2011, effective
275 September 14, 2011 (D.C. Law 19-21; D.C. Official Code § 10-551.01 et. seq.), is amended by
276 adding a new section 1028i to read as follows:
277 “Sec. 1028i. Recreational facilities assessment.
278 “(a) The Department shall conduct an annual survey to update information on the
279 condition of spray parks, artificial turf fields, playgrounds, and courts such as tennis, pickleball,
280 basketball, or other similar hard surface courts, as determined by the Department, at recreational
281 facilities. The survey results shall be disaggregated by facility, made publicly available, and
282 transmitted to the Council, the Council chairpersons with oversight jurisdiction over the
283 Department and the Department of Parks and Recreation, and the Office of the City
284 Administrator by March 1 of each year.
285 “(b) For the purposes of this section, the term “recreation facility” shall have the same
286 meaning as set forth in section 1028c(a)(2).”.
287
14

288 SUBTITLE E. HUMAN SERVICES GRANT ADMINISTRATION
289 Sec. 1041. Short title.
290 This subtitle may be cited as the “Human Services Grant Administration Congressional
291 Review Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
292 Sec. 1042. The Grant Administration Act of 2013, effective December 24, 2013 (D.C.
293 Law 20-61; D.C. Official Code § 1-328.11 et seq.), is amended by adding a new section 1099 to
294 read as follows:
295 “Sec. 1099. Human Services grants.
296 “(a) For grants, the grant agreements for which are received by the Department of Human
297 Services (“DHS”) signed by the grantee after October 1, 2026, that are funded exclusively by
298 local operating funds, and for which DHS is the sole grantor (“DHS local grants”), the first
299 payment to the grantee under the grant shall issue no later than 30 days following the start of the
300 fiscal year or other term of service during which the grantee must perform under its grant
301 agreement with DHS or no later than 30 days following the actual receipt by DHS of a signed
302 grant agreement, whichever is later.
303 “(b) DHS shall provide the grant agreement for each DHS local grant to the grantee for
304 the grantee’s review and signature no later than 30 days following the start of the fiscal year or
305 other term of service during which the grantee must perform under its grant agreement with
306 DHS.”.

308 SUBTITLE F. ANC FUNDING FLEXIBILITY CLARIFICATION
309 Sec. 1051. Short title.
310 This subtitle may be cited as the “Advisory Neighborhood Commissions Funding
311 Flexibility Clarification Congressional Review Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
312 Sec. 1052. Section 16 of the Advisory Neighborhood Commissions Act of 1975, effective
313 March 26, 1976 (D.C. Law 1-58; D.C. Official Code § 1-309.13), is amended as follows:
314 (a) Subsection (b)(1) is amended as follows:
315 (1) The existing text is redesignated as subparagraph (A).
316 (2) A new subparagraph (B) is added to read as follows:
317 “(B) Every such commercial bank, savings and loan association, credit
318 union, or combination thereof, shall provide to the Office of the Chief Financial Officer at
319 oft.bankingservices@dc.gov, on a monthly or quarterly basis, depending on the frequency with
320 which each such financial institution issues such records in the ordinary course of business, a
321 copy of the account statement of each Commission for which it serves as a depository of all
322 funds received, or online access to the same.”.
323 (b) Subsection (d)(1) is amended by striking the phrase “to the Council” and inserting the
324 phrase “to the Council and the OANC” in its place.
325 (c) Subsection (f)(2A)(C) is repealed.
326 (d) A new subsection (f-1) is added to read as follows:
327 “(f-1) A record or signature by an officer of a Commission who has authority to
16

328 sign on behalf of the Commission may be in electronic form.”.
329 (e) Subsection (h) is repealed.
330 (f) Subsection (l)(3) is repealed.
331 (g) Subsection (l-1)(3)(B)(i) is amended by striking the phrase “Authority;” and
332 inserting the phrase “Authority, and expenses for transportation by the use of a taxicab or
333 rideshare vehicle;” in its place.
334 (h) A new subsection (m-1) is added to read as follows:
335 “(m-1) Any services funded by a direct expenditure from a Commission must not be
336 duplicative of any services that are already performed by the District government.”.
337 (i) Subsection (q) is amended by striking the phrase “may seek to reprogram” and
338 inserting the phrase “shall provide” in its place.
339 SUBTITLE G. COMMUNITY LEGAL EDUCATION AND RESOURCES GRANT
340 PROGRAM
341 Sec. 1061. Short title.
342 This subtitle may be cited as the “Community Legal Education and Resources Grant
343 Congressional Review Emergency Act of 2025”.
344 Sec. 1062. Community legal education and resources grant program.
345 (a) There is established a Community Legal Education and Resources Grant Program
346 (“Program”) to be administered by the Mayor to provide grants, pursuant to the Grant
17

347 Administration Act of 2013, effective December 24, 2013 (D.C. Law 20-61; D.C. Official Code §
348 1-328.11 et seq.), to legal services providers to deliver legal services.
349 (b) The Mayor, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure
350 Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code Section § 2-501 et seq.), may
351 issue rules to implement the Program, including rules governing the:
352 (1) Types of legal services projects eligible for grant funding;
353 (2) Application process and timing; and
354 (3) Monitoring of Program performance and reporting requirements.
355 (c) For the purposes of this subtitle, the term:
356 (1) “Legal services” means:
357 (A) Legal representation of District residents, including through the
358 provision of legal advice, brief services, and limited-scope representation; or
359 (B) Training of attorneys in legal issues.
360 (2) “Legal services provider” means:
361 (A) A nonprofit organization;
362 (B) A private entity that partners with a nonprofit organization; or
363 (C) A private entity utilizing pro bono legal assistance.
364 SUBTITLE H. ACCOUNTABILITY FOR BUDGET DELAYS
365 Sec. 1071. Short title.
18

366 This subtitle may be cited as the “Accountability for Delaying the Budget Congressional
367 Review Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
368 Sec. 1072. If the Mayor submits an annual budget later than the date established by the
369 Council pursuant to section 442(a) of the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved
370 December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 798; D.C. Official Code § 1-204.42(a)), nonpersonnel services
371 spending shall be prohibited within the Executive Office of the Mayor and the Office of the City
372 Administrator until the day after the date on which the Mayor submits the annual budget to the
373 Council.
374 Sec. 1073. Section 47-363(b)(3) of the District of Columbia Official Code is amended by
375 striking the phrase “is on recess.” and inserting the phrase “is on recess. If the Mayor submits an
376 annual budget later than the date established by the Council pursuant to § 1-204.42(a), no request
377 may be submitted to the Chairman of the Council under this subsection until after the date on
378 which the Mayor submits the annual budget to the Council.” in its place.
379 Sec. 1074. Section 711 of the Rules of Organization and Procedure for the Council of the
380 District of Columbia, Council Period 26, Resolution of 2025, effective January 2, 2025 (Res. 26-
381 1; 72 DCR 1289), is amended to read as follows:
382 “711. EFFECT OF RECESS AND BUDGET SUBMISSION DELAY ON
383 PROCEDURES.
19

384 “(a) Reprogramming requests and grant budget modification requests may not be
385 submitted to the Council during a recess of the Council. No time period provided in this part for
386 the consideration of the requests will continue to run during a recess of the Council.
387 “(b) If the Mayor submits an annual budget later than the date established by the Council
388 pursuant to section 442(a) of the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved December 24,
389 1973 (87 Stat. 798; D.C. Official Code § 1-204.42(a)), reprogramming requests and grant budget
390 modification requests may not be submitted to the Council until after the date on which the
391 Mayor submits the annual budget to the Council.”.

529 SUBTITLE F. RFK CAMPUS INFRASTRUCTURE FUND
530 Sec. 2051. Short title.
531 This subtitle may be cited as the “RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund Establishment
532 Congressional Review Emergency Act of 2025”.
533 Sec. 2052. RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund.
534 (a) There is established as a special fund the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund, which
535 shall be administered by the Mayor pursuant to subsections (c), (d), and (e) of this section.
27

536 (b) After all principal and interest on the bonds issued pursuant to section 103 of the
537 Ballpark Omnibus Financing and Revenue Act of 2004, effective April 8, 2005 (D.C. Law 15-
538 320; D.C. Official Code § 10-1601.03), has been paid, all receipts from the sports facilities fee
539 imposed by D.C. Official Code § 47-2762 shall be deposited into the RFK Campus Infrastructure
540 Fund.
541 (c) Money in the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund shall be used:
542 (1) To pay the debt service, including principal and interest, costs of issuance, and
543 credit enhancements, and any costs of defeasance on bonds issued for RFK campus infrastructure
544 and parking facilities, and to make any other payments related to such bonds;
545 (2) To fund reserves for bonds issued for RFK campus infrastructure and parking
546 facilities; and
547 (3) For the purposes set forth in and in accordance with subsection (d) of this
548 section.
549 (d) Any money available in the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund in excess of the
550 amounts required to be paid or reserved pursuant to subsection (c)(1) and (2) of this section, as
551 determined by the Chief Financial Officer, shall:
552 (1) In Fiscal Years 2026 and 2027:
553 (A) Be used to pay the debt service on any ballpark early redemption
554 borrowing; and
28

555 (B) To the extent all debt service on any ballpark early redemption
556 borrowing has been paid, be transferred to the General Fund of the District of Columbia;
557 (2) In Fiscal Years 2028 and 2029, be transferred to the General Fund of the
558 District of Columbia;
559 (3)(A) In Fiscal Year 2030 and each fiscal year thereafter, be transferred to the
560 RFK Transportation Improvement Fund, established in the Robert F. Kennedy Campus
561 Redevelopment Act of 2025, passed on 1st reading on August 1, 2025(Engrossed version of Bill
562 26-288).
563 (B) If the amount of an annual deposit to the RFK Transportation
564 Improvement Fund pursuant to subparagraph (A) of this paragraph would exceed $20 million,
565 $20 million shall be deposited in the RFK Transportation Fund and the amount over $20 million
566 shall be deposited in the General Fund of the District of Columbia.
567 (e) The Mayor, or any District instrumentality or authority designated by the Mayor, may
568 pledge and create a security interest in the funds in the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund for the
569 payment of the debt service on any bonds issued for RFK campus infrastructure and parking
570 facilities, any fees and charges incurred in connection therewith, and any payments owing under
571 any document or instrument entered into in connection with such indebtedness in accordance
572 with the provisions of the documents entered into by the District in connection with the issuance
573 of such bonds.
29

574 (f)(1) Except as provided in subsection (d)(3)(B) of this section, the money deposited into
575 the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund shall not revert to the unrestricted fund balance of the
576 General Fund of the District of Columbia at the end of a fiscal year, or at any other time.
577 (2) Subject to authorization in an approved budget and financial plan, any funds
578 appropriated in the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund shall be continually available without
579 regard to fiscal year limitation.
580 (g) For the purposes of this section, the term “RFK campus” means the parcels of land
581 that are the subject of the Transfer of Jurisdiction Plat recorded in the Surveyor’s Office of the
582 District of Columbia on February 5, 2025, on page 13 of subdivision book 223, together with any
583 public streets within or adjacent to such parcels that may be closed from time to time.

652 consecutively numbered from 1 to 75, and the bingo cards held by the players, which cards are

667 “(C) Bingo played over the internet or in an online environment or on any
668 machine or mechanical device that would qualify as or constitute a facsimile of class II gaming,
669 as that term is defined in section 4(7) of the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act, approved October 17,

1023 SUBTITLE L. TRUXTON CIRCLE EMINENT DOMAIN AUTHORITY
1024 Sec. 2111. Short title.
1025 This subtitle may be cited as the “Truxton Circle Eminent Domain Authority
1026 Congressional Review Emergency Act of 2025”.
1027 Sec. 2112. The Council finds that:
1028 (1) The Truxton Circle neighborhood is a mixed-use neighborhood characterized
1029 by mixed-density residential, commercial, and retail uses. It is a high-priority corridor for
1030 investment, in-fill development, and the revitalization of vacant and underutilized lots.
1031 (2) Lot 48 in Square 3100 (“the Property”), located at approximately 1600 North
1032 Capitol Street, NW, is approximately 18,984 square feet and located at the northwest intersection
1033 of North Capitol Street, NW, and Florida Avenue, NW. It is bounded by North Capitol Street,
1034 NW, to the east, Q Street, NW, to the south, and Florida Avenue, NW, to the west.
1035 (3) The property is at the intersection of 2 major District corridors and
1036 development of these areas is a high-priority measure for the District and residents of Ward 5.
53

1037 (4) The property presents the opportunity for redevelopment along North Capitol
1038 Street, NW, and a reduction in blight. This parcel is ripe for matter-of-right, neighborhood-
1039 appropriate development, including housing, retail, mixed-use development, and office space.
1040 (5) Acquisition of the property by the District will allow for development to
1041 invigorate a vacant and underutilized parcel and to reposition the property for development and
1042 revitalization.
1043 Sec. 2113. The Mayor may exercise eminent domain in accordance with the procedures
1044 set forth in Subchapter II of Chapter 13 of Title 16 of the District of Columbia Official Code to
1045 acquire Lot 48 in Square 3100 for the purpose of revitalization or redevelopment.

1080 Sec. 2132. (a) Pursuant to section 404 of the District of Columbia Home Rule Act,
1081 approved December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 803; D.C. Official Code § 1-204.04), and consistent with
1082 section 1 of An Act To authorize the transfer of public land in the District of Columbia, approved

1084 Columbia authorizes the transfer of jurisdiction from the Director of the National Park Service,
1085 acting on behalf of the Secretary of the Interior, to the government of the District of Columbia,
1086 over a portion of U.S. Reservation 339, which is National Park Service Land and appurtenant
1087 facilities in Rock Creek Park, the boundaries of which are generally Kennedy Place, NW, to the
1088 north; 16th Street, NW, and Colorado Avenue, NW, to the east; the inside boundary of the
1089 existing parking lots to the south and west; Stage Road, NW, to the west; and a portion of
1090 Morrow Drive, NW, to the existing tree line to where it intersects with Kennedy Place, NW, to
1091 the west, upon which is situated the Rock Creek Tennis Center and appurtenant facilities, as
1092 shown on a plat to be drawn and filed in the Office of the Surveyor of the District of Columbia.
1093 (b) Upon the transfer of jurisdiction described in subsection (a) of this section, or another
1094 transfer of jurisdiction approved by the Council pursuant to section 1 of An Act To authorize the
1095 transfer of jurisdiction over public land in the District of Columbia, approved May 20, 1932 (47
1096 Stat. 161; D.C. Official Code § 10-111), over the property in which the Rock Creek Tennis
56

1097 Center is situated, the Department of Parks and Recreation shall commence the Rock Creek
1098 Tennis Center capital project to make improvements necessary to bring the existing tennis center
1099 into compliance with Association of Tennis Professionals Tour and Women’s Tennis
1100 Association Tour event standards.
1101 Sec. 2133. It is the sense of the Council that the Mayor, in accepting a transfer of
1102 jurisdiction that includes the Rock Creek Tennis Center, should:
1103 (1) Thoroughly and thoughtfully engage with the communities and organizations
1104 impacted by the current and future uses of the property over which jurisdiction is to be
1105 transferred, including Advisory Neighborhood Commission 4E, the Rock Creek Conservancy,
1106 and residents of the Sixteenth Street Heights and Crestwood neighborhoods.
1107 (2) Provide a reasonable period of time for public comment, including
1108 opportunities for Executive agencies to answer public questions about the transfer of jurisdiction.
1109 (3) Incorporate any relevant environmental, traffic, and noise impact studies
1110 previously completed pertaining to the property over which jurisdiction is to be transferred, or
1111 conduct additional studies of comparable rigor and scope that should be made available to the
1112 public.
1113 (4) Prioritize preservation of open and free access to as much of the property over
1114 which jurisdiction is to be transferred as possible for as much of the year as possible, including
1115 the existing Picnic Grove #24 and public parking spaces to be utilized for public access of other
1116 areas of Rock Creek Park.
57

1117 (5) Explore the role of the Carter Barron Amphitheater in a proposed or future
1118 transfer of jurisdiction to ensure preservation, improvement, and future productive public use of
1119 this historic community asset.
1120 SUBTITLE O. HISTORIC BURIAL GROUNDS PRESERVATION PROGRAM
1121 Sec. 2141. Short title.
1122 This subtitle may be cited as the “Historic Burial Grounds Preservation Program
1123 Congressional Review Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
1124 Sec. 2142. The Historic Landmark and Historic District Protection Act of 1978, effective
1125 March 3, 1979 (D.C. Law 2-144; D.C. Official Code § 6-1101 et seq.), is amended by adding a
1126 new section 11c to read as follows:
1127 “Sec. 11c. Paul E. Sluby, Sr. Historic Burial Grounds Preservation Program.
1128 “(a) There is established a Paul E. Sluby, Sr. Historic Burial Grounds Preservation
1129 Program at the Office of Planning (“Office”).
1130 “(b) Subject to available funding, the Office shall issue grants to qualified charitable
1131 organizations for the following purposes:
1132 (1) The preservation and restoration of historic burial grounds;
1133 (2) The identification of historic burial grounds;
1134 (3) The interpretation of historic burial grounds;
1135 (4) The repatriation of human remains, particularly those from former historic
1136 burial grounds; or
58

1137 (5) Related research and documentation of historic burial grounds including burial
1138 records, locational data, and contested ownership.
1139 “(c) Qualified charitable organizations that seek a grant for activities at a historic burial
1140 ground that is located on private property shall be considered for a grant only with the written
1141 consent of the property owner.
1142 “(d) For the purposes of this section, the term:
1143 “(1) “Historic burial ground” means a cemetery or any natural or prepared
1144 physical location, whether originally below, on, or above the surface of the earth, into which
1145 human remains are deposited as a part of the death rite or ceremony of a culture, and that was
1146 established in the District of Columbia prior to January 1, 1955, for interments of African
1147 Americans and is owned by a public body or qualified charitable organization.
1148 “(2) “Qualified charitable organization” means a charitable corporation, charitable
1149 association, or charitable trust that has been granted tax-exempt status under § 501(c)(3) of the
1150 Internal Revenue Code and that has the primary purpose of preserving historical cemeteries and
1151 graves or was formed for the purpose of identifying, preserving, or maintaining historic burial
1152 grounds.”.

1243 SUBTITLE R. EVENTS DC GRANTS
1244 Sec. 2171. Short title.
1245 This subtitle may be cited as the “Events DC Grants Congressional Review Emergency
1246 Act of 2025”.
1247 Sec. 2172. National Cherry Blossom Festival grant.
1248 (a) There is established a matching grant program to support the 2026 National Cherry
1249 Blossom Festival (“Program”), which shall be administered by the Washington Convention and
1250 Sports Authority (“Events DC”). Under the Program, a matching grant shall be awarded to a
1251 nonprofit organization that organizes and produces an event or events as part of the official,
1252 month-long National Cherry Blossom Festival (“Festival”) at a rate of $2 for every dollar that the
1253 organization has raised in corporate donations by April 30, 2026; except, that the total matching
1254 grant shall not exceed $1.5 million.
64

1255 (b) In Fiscal Year 2026, of the funds allocated to the Non-Departmental Account, $1.5
1256 million shall be transferred to Events DC to use for the grant authorized by subsection (a) of this
1257 section.
1258 (c) A grant awarded pursuant to this section shall be in addition to any other grant
1259 awarded by Events DC in support of the Festival.
1260 Sec. 2173. DC History grants.
1261 (a) In Fiscal Year 2026, Events DC shall issue a grant of no less than $350,000 for the
1262 purpose of providing funds to a nonprofit organization located in the District that
1263 provides education about how the District of Columbia has been the home for the fight for
1264 freedom and democracy, with an emphasis on including the entire District across all 8 wards in
1265 this history.
1266 (b)(1) In Fiscal Year 2026, Events DC shall issue a grant of no less than $250,000 to a
1267 nonprofit organization occupying space in the Carnegie Library building that is engaged in
1268 collecting, interpreting, and sharing the history of the District.
1269 (2) A grant awarded pursuant to this subsection shall be in addition to any other
1270 grant awarded by Events DC in support of historical education and research.

1346 SUBTITLE V. INTERACTIVE WAYFINDING KIOSKS
1347 Sec. 2211. Short title.
1348 This subtitle may be cited as the “Interactive Wayfinding Kiosk Congressional Review
1349 Emergency Act of 2025”.
1350 Sec. 2212. Definitions.
1351 For the purposes of this subtitle, the term:
1352 (1) “Commercial district” means the geographic area included in the boundaries
1353 of BID corporations, as that term is defined in section 3(4) of the Business Improvement
69

1354 Districts Act of 1996, effective May 29, 1996 (D.C. Law 11-134; D.C. Official Code § 2-
1355 1215.02(4)), and of Main Street corridors.
1356 (2) “Interactive wayfinding kiosk” means an interactive informational wayfinding
1357 platform for use by pedestrians and erected in the public right-of-way on public space in the form
1358 of a kiosk capable of providing or generating wireless internet at no cost to users and
1359 electronically displayed content including weather updates, multimodal mapping to event
1360 destinations with mobile integration, shopping, dining, and medical points of interest, job
1361 postings, real time transportation information, public opinion surveys, camera enabled
1362 technology for public safety use, public safety and police emergency notifications and call button
1363 functionality, kiosk usage information, public service announcements, and digital commercial
1364 advertisements.
1365 (3) “Unrestricted locations” means areas of public space, including commercial
1366 districts, where the installation of interactive wayfinding kiosks is not prohibited by law or
1367 regulation.
1368 Sec. 2213. Authorization for master license agreement.
1369 The Mayor is authorized to enter into a contract with a provider of interactive wayfinding
1370 kiosks (“provider”) to install and operate interactive wayfinding kiosks in commercial districts
1371 and other unrestricted locations in the District; provided, that:
1372 (1) The District receives a percentage of the revenue derived from any
1373 commercial digital advertisements displayed on interactive wayfinding kiosks in the District; and
70

1374 (2) The master license agreement between the Mayor and the provider complies
1375 with any other terms established by law or regulation.
1376 Sec. 2214. Rules.
1377 The Mayor, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure Act,
1378 approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Code § 2-501 et seq.), may issue rules
1379 governing interactive wayfinding kiosks in the District, including rules related to their design,
1380 placement, and component parts.

1560 SUBTITLE E. BACKGROUND CHECK AND RAP BACK PROGRAM
1561 Sec. 3041. Short title.
1562 This subtitle may be cited as the “Background Check Fingerprinting Authority and Rap
1563 Back Program Congressional Review Emergency Act of 2025”.
1564 Sec. 3042. Definitions.
1565 For the purposes of this subtitle, the term:
1566 (1) “Covered individual” means an individual who has submitted to a fingerprint-
1567 based background check as a condition of caring for children, persons with a disability, the
1568 elderly, or vulnerable adults, a security officer, special police officer, private detective, private
1569 detective agency, security agency, or other person responsible for protecting property, preventing
80

1570 theft, damage to real or personal property, assaults, disorder, or other illegal occurrences, or for
1571 purposes of licensure, appointment, commission, certification, registration, employment, or
1572 volunteer service with a participating agency pursuant to District law or regulation.
1573 (2) “FBI” means the Federal Bureau of Investigation.
1574 (3) “FBI Rap Back Service” means the FBI Next Generation Identification
1575 Record of Arrest and Prosecution Background Service.
1576 (4) “MPD” means the Metropolitan Police Department.
1577 (5) “Notification event” means an event, such as an arrest or other criminal
1578 activity when fingerprints are taken, that triggers a notification from the FBI Rap Back Service to
1579 the Metropolitan Police Department regarding a covered individual who has been subscribed to
1580 the FBI Rap Back Service.
1581 (6) “Participating agency” means a District government agency that requires a
1582 fingerprint-based background check and receives the results as a condition of caring for children,
1583 persons with a disability, the elderly, or vulnerable adults, a security officer, special police
1584 officer, private detective, private detective agency, security agency, or other person responsible
1585 for protecting property, preventing theft, damage to real or personal property, assaults, disorder,
1586 or similar illegal occurrences, or for purposes of licensure, appointment, commission,
1587 certification, registration, employment, or volunteer service.
1588 Sec. 3043. Background check fingerprinting authority.
81

1589 (a) If the fingerprinting of an individual is required or authorized by any District or
1590 federal law or regulation for the purposes of conducting a background check of the individual,
1591 MPD, or an entity authorized by MPD, may fingerprint the individual, forward the fingerprints to
1592 the FBI for the purpose of conducting a criminal history check, receive the results of the criminal
1593 history check, and disseminate the results of the criminal history check to entities authorized to
1594 receive the results.
1595 (b) The authority provided by this section applies to fingerprinting authorized under the
1596 District of Columbia Rap Back Program and to fingerprinting required or authorized by any
1597 other District or federal law or regulation.
1598 Sec. 3044. District of Columbia Rap Back Program.
1599 (a) MPD shall participate on behalf of the District in the FBI Rap Back Service through
1600 the establishment of a District of Columbia Rap Back Program.
1601 (b) The purpose of the District of Columbia Rap Back Program shall be to allow
1602 participating agencies, through the District of Columbia Rap Back Program, to subscribe covered
1603 individuals in the FBI Rap Back Service and to be notified when a covered individual is the
1604 subject of an FBI Rap Back Service notification event.
1605 (c) If a participating agency requests that the District of Columbia Rap Back Program
1606 subscribe a covered individual in the FBI Rap Back Service, the covered individual shall be
1607 fingerprinted by MPD or an entity authorized by MPD and the fingerprints shall be forwarded by
82

1608 MPD to the FBI for a national criminal history check and subscription in the FBI Rap Back
1609 Service.
1610 (d) MPD shall notify the relevant participating agency when a covered individual
1611 subscribed by the participating agency in the FBI Rap Back Service through the District of
1612 Columbia Rap Back Program is the subject of an FBI Rap Back Service notification event.
1613 (e) For the purposes of administering the District of Columbia Rap Back Program and
1614 performing or facilitating criminal history background screenings, MPD is authorized to take the
1615 fingerprints of a covered individual, submit to the FBI the fingerprints of, and accompanying
1616 records regarding, a covered individual, and allow such fingerprints and records to be retained by
1617 the FBI Rap Back Service and used for ongoing searches through the FBI Rap Back Service.
1618 Sec. 3045. Limitation on use of information.
1619 The information contained in a notification event received by a participating agency shall
1620 be used by the participating agency only for the purpose of determining a covered individual’s
1621 eligibility to care for children, persons with a disability, the elderly, or vulnerable adults, a
1622 security officer, special police officer, private detective, private detective agency, security
1623 agency, or other person responsible for protecting property, preventing theft, damage to real or
1624 personal property, assaults, disorders, or similar illegal occurrences, or for purposes of licensure,
1625 appointment, commission, certification, registration, employment, or volunteer service and shall
1626 not be further disseminated by the participating agency.
1627 Sec. 3046. Fees.
83

1628 MPD may establish by rule a fee, to be imposed on a covered individual or participating
1629 agency, for subscription of a covered individual in the District of Columbia Rap Back
1630 Program. The fee may be imposed on an annual basis.
1631 Sec. 3047. Rules.
1632 MPD, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure Act,
1633 approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), may issue rules
1634 to govern the implementation of the District of Columbia Rap Back Program and to otherwise
1635 implement the provisions of this subtitle.
1636 SUBTITLE F. DETAINERS
1637 Sec. 3051. Short title.

1804 Sec. 4022. (a) In School Year 2025-2026, the Office of the State Superintendent of

1806 Investments account to public charter LEAs to increase the compensation of public charter
1807 school educators.

1809 LEA’s chief executive officer or head of school shall sign an assurance that the funds provided
1810 under this section will be:
1811 (1) Used exclusively to increase the compensation of public charter school
1812 educators; and
1813 (2) Paid to the public charter LEA’s educators during School Year 2025-2026.

1815 (1) “Public charter LEA” means an individual public charter school or a group of
1816 public charter schools operating under a single charter.
99

1817 (2) “Educator” means a school-based employee who directly supports students,

1819 teachers, instructional coaches, athletic trainers, attendance coordinators, counselors, physical
1820 therapists, social workers, school psychologists, speech therapists, librarians, and classroom

1822 personnel such as principals, assistant principals, deans, and office staff.

2095 education program or a school that hosts a dual-language education program;
116

2096 “(B) Embedding a dual-language education program into an existing

2100 establish a dual-language education campus at Shirley Chisholm Elementary School; and
2101 “(D) Incorporating Ward 6, 7, and 8 dual-language education public
2102 charter school elementary schools without an existing or nearby middle school feeder into a
2103 District of Columbia Public Schools dual-language education program or middle school feeder
2104 pattern;

2106 on the following considerations:
2107 “(A) Capital and operational costs;
2108 “(B) Staffing requirements and models;
2109 “(C) The transportation time of the students and families likely to attend
2110 the new school or program;
2111 “(D) The impact on enrollment patterns of the elementary and middle
2112 schools in the proposed or existing feeder patterns; and

2114 boundary status, to attend such a dual-language program or school;
117

2115 “(3) Analyze the demand in Wards 7 and 8 for a dual-language education middle-
2116 grade option, which shall include:

2705 increasing, clearly defined schedule of wages;

2708 “(IV) Provides collaborative professional development

2748 “(v) Access to out-of-school programming, including enrollment in
2749 and transportation to afterschool activities;
2750 “(vi) Mentorship programming; and
2751 “(vii) Any such other services to address identified needs for the
2752 purposes of preventing youth from committing further offenses; and
2753 “(B) Include close coordination with the Department to implement aspects
2754 of discharge and reentry plans described in D.C. Official Code § 16-2320(i).
2755 “(4) Preference shall be granted to applicants:
2756 “(A) Based in the District of Columbia or with a mission of primarily
2757 serving residents of the District of Columbia; and
2758 “(B) With a demonstrated history of partnership with the District of
2759 Columbia government, including receiving District-funded grant awards within the past 5 years,
150

2760 having current or prior MOUs with a District agency within the past 5 years, or entering into
2761 partnerships with the Department within the past 5 years.
2762 “(5) Within 14 months of receiving a grant issued pursuant to this subsection, a
2763 recipient shall submit to the Department and the Council a report that describes, at a minimum:
2764 “(A) The number of youth served, by age and Ward residence;
2765 “(B) The services received by participants;
2766 “(C) Outcomes by type of service rendered to participants;
2767 “(D) The number of school-aged participants who are enrolled in school or
2768 a GED program;
2769 “(E) The number of non-school-aged participants who are enrolled in
2770 postsecondary education; and
2771 “(F) The number of non-school-aged participants who are employed full
2772 or part time.
2773 “(6) Within 14 months of issuing any grant pursuant to this subsection, the
2774 Department shall submit to the Office of the Attorney General and the Council committee with
2775 jurisdiction over the Department a report disclosing for each youth participant any known
2776 involvement with law enforcement or return to Department custody during the duration of the
2777 grant period, subject to juvenile confidentiality laws.”.

3167 “Sec. 3a. Long-Term Care Strategic Coordinator.
3168 “There is established within the Office of the Deputy Mayor for Health and Human
3169 Services (“DMHHS”) the position of the Long-Term Care Strategic Coordinator
3170 (“Coordinator”), who shall be a full-time employee of the District. By January 1, 2026, the
3171 Coordinator shall be responsible for:
3172 “(1) Coordinating the Age-Friendly DC program;
3173 “(2) Tracking the long-term care services provided by agencies under the purview
3174 of DMHHS (“health agencies”);
3175 “(3) Using data to develop a strategy to improve and increase the capacity of the
3176 long-term care services workforce to meet the District’s needs;
3177 “(4) Identifying points of contact within each relevant agency outside of the
3178 health agencies, including the Deputy Mayor for Education and the Department for Aging and
3179 Community Living, to avoid duplication of work across agencies and to ensure each agency’s
3180 work aligns with the broader mission of supporting the District’s aging population and long-term
3181 care workforce; and
3182 “(5) Carrying out other duties relevant to support the long-term care workforce as
3183 may be identified and assigned by DMHHS.”.

3333 SUBTITLE X. BODY ART REGULATION CLARIFICATION
3334 Sec. 5231. Short title.
3335 This subtitle may be cited as the “Body Art Regulation Clarification Congressional
3336 Review Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
3337 Sec. 5232. Section 47-2853.76b of the District of Columbia Official Code is amended as
3338 follows:
3339 (a) Subsection (a) is amended as follows:
3340 (1) The lead-in language is amended as follows:
3341 (A) Strike the phrase “, through the Board of Barber and Cosmetology,
3342 shall regulate” and insert the phrase “shall regulate” in its place.
180

3343 (B) Strike the phrase “offered by:” and insert the phrase “offered by
3344 establishing and imposing occupational licensing, registration requirements, and associated fee
3345 schedules.” in its place.
3346 (2) Paragraphs (1) and (2) are repealed.
3347 (b) New subsections (b), (c), and (d) are added to read as follows:
3348 “(b) The Department of Health shall regulate body art establishments to ensure that such
3349 establishments have adequate health, sanitization, sterilization and safety methods, procedures,
3350 equipment, and supplies by establishing minimum sterilization, sanitation, health, and safety
3351 standards for the operation of such establishments as may be necessary to prevent infection and
3352 contamination of equipment, supplies, or work surfaces with pathogenic organisms and by
3353 establishing and imposing operational licensing, registration requirements, and associated fee
3354 schedules.
3355 “(c)(1) All body art establishments offering tattooing procedures shall conspicuously post
3356 a written disclosure that states the following:
3357 “The United States Food and Drug Administration has not approved any pigment color
3358 additive for injectable use as tattoo ink. There may be a risk of carcinogenic decomposition
3359 associated with certain pigments when the pigments are subsequently exposed to concentrated
3360 ultra-violet light or laser irradiation.
3361 “(2) All body art establishments offering tattooing procedures shall maintain
3362 documentation on the premises containing the following information and shall disclose such
181

3363 information to customers upon request:
3364 “(A) The components of the pigments used in the body art establishment;
3365 “(B) The names, addresses, and telephone numbers of the suppliers and
3366 manufacturers of pigments used in the body art establishment for the past 3 years; and
3367 “(C) Identification of any recalled pigments used in the establishment for
3368 the past 3 years and the supplier and manufacturer of each pigment.
3369 “(3) All body art establishments shall maintain and use regularly calibrated
3370 autoclave equipment for the sterilization of any non-disposable body art equipment at a
3371 frequency to be established by the Department of Health.
3372 “(4) Only single-use disposable sharps, pigments, gloves, and cleansing products
3373 shall be used in connection with body art procedures in body art establishments, in accordance
3374 with rules established by the Department of Health pursuant to subsection (b) of this section.
3375 “(5) A body art establishment that is in violation of this subsection shall be
3376 subject to license suspension or revocation and a maximum fine of $2,500.
3377 “(d)(1) No person shall operate a body art establishment or perform body art procedures
3378 in a body art establishment unless that establishment has obtained a valid body art establishment
3379 license issued by the Mayor.
3380 “(2) No body art establishment shall employ or permit body artists to perform
3381 body art procedures in the body art establishment unless the body artist holds a valid body art
3382 license issued by the Mayor.
182

3383 “(3) Any person violating paragraph (1) or (2) of this subsection shall, upon
3384 conviction, be guilty of a misdemeanor and may be punished by a fine not exceeding $2,500,
3385 imprisonment for not more than 3 months, or both.”.

3835 SUBTITLE M. CLEAN CITY OFFICE ESTABLISHMENT
3836 Sec. 6121. Short title.
3837 This subtitle may be cited as the “Clean City Office Establishment Congressional Review
3838 Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
3839 Sec. 6122. Title I of the Sustainable Solid Waste Management Amendment Act of 2014,
3840 effective February 26, 2015 (D.C. Law 20-154; D.C. Official Code § 8-1031.01 et seq.), is
3841 amended by adding a new subtitle C to read as follows:
3842 “SUBTITLE C. Office of the Clean City.
3843 “Sec. 127. Establishment of the Office of the Clean City.
3844 “(a) There is established within the Department of Public Works the Office of the Clean
3845 City, which shall be headed by a full-time Clean City Coordinator, who shall be appointed by the
3846 Mayor.
208

3847 “(b) The Clean City Coordinator shall:
3848 “(1) Conduct cleanliness assessments on a quarterly basis for the entire District
3849 and on an as-needed basis for the District of Columbia National Highway System and provide
3850 written reports and GIS maps documenting the outcomes of those assessments;
3851 “(2) Work in partnership and consultation with the various agencies and offices
3852 that have cleanliness and beautification operational responsibility to develop, coordinate and
3853 support Clean City program activities and to deliver Clean City services;
3854 “(3) Develop, coordinate, and support Clean City program activities with agency
3855 divisions that have operational responsibility for maintaining the cleanliness of the District;
3856 “(4) Work with agency directors and staff to identify and resolve barriers to
3857 effective cooperation among multiple agencies to further the cleanliness of the District in areas,
3858 including financial, legal, or procurement services;
3859 “(5) Assist the Director of the Department of Public Works and the Office of
3860 Waste Diversion with innovations in public and household solid-waste container infrastructure
3861 and collections;
3862 “(6) Advocate for the enforcement of existing laws and municipal regulations that
3863 can have a positive impact on the cleanliness and appearance of the District;
3864 “(7) Solicit the involvement of ANCs, civic associations, concerned citizens, and
3865 businesses in litter-prevention programs and support for the cleaning of the District;
209

3866 “(8) Maintain a website containing information on Clean City activities,
3867 education, and community engagement information;
3868 “(9) Develop and support Clean City Initiative programs to educate and engage
3869 District of Columbia Public Schools and Public Charter School students in litter-prevention
3870 programs and support for the cleaning of the District;
3871 “(10) Formulate and implement a fundraising strategy to solicit corporate and
3872 foundation contributions towards Clean City Initiatives, including “Adopt-A-Block” programs;
3873 “(11) Support the coordination of rodent-abatement programs between the
3874 Department of Public Works and Department of Health; and
3875 “(12) Support planning and resource allocation for pet-waste disposal.
3876 “(c) Subject to funding, the Clean City Coordinator may issue grants to support public-
3877 space cleaning efforts. Such grants shall:
3878 “(1) Preference supporting and expanding the service area of existing Clean
3879 Teams funded by the Department of Small and Local Business Development;
3880 “(2) Prioritize public space cleaning for major arterials, commercial corridors, and
3881 mixed-use neighborhoods; and
3882 “(3) Not be used to replace work performed by Department of Public Works
3883 staff.”.

5081 “(a) For the purpose of this section, the term:
5082 “(1) “Owner” means McMillan Parcel 2 Owner, LLC, and McMillan Parcel 4
5083 Owner, LLC, affiliates of LDP Holdings, LLC d/b/a Jair Lynch Real Estate Partners, and its

5086 thereon, at Parcel 2 West and Parcel 4 within the Reservoir District; known for tax and
5087 assessment purposes as Lots 814 and 815 in Square 3128, and Lots 809 and 810 in Square 3128,
5088 respectively.

5090 Property pursuant to Chapter 8 of this title shall be exempted for 20 real property tax years;
5091 provided, that the Owner shall:
5092 “(1) Operate or cause to be operated 449 units of housing at the Property;
275

5093 “(2) Set aside 1/3 of the operating rental housing units in the Property as
5094 affordable and available for households earning an average of 80% of the Area Median Income;
5095 “(3) Enter into an agreement with the District government that requires the
5096 Owner, or its designee or assignee, to, at a minimum, contract with certified business enterprises
5097 for at least 35% of the contract dollar volume of the construction of the project on the Property,
5098 in accordance with Subchapter IX-A of Chapter 2 of Title 2; and
5099 “(4) By September 30 of the year immediately preceding each tax year in the
5100 exemption period set forth in this subsection, provide the Mayor with information showing what
5101 percentage of each of the requirements for eligibility for the exemption provided in paragraphs
5102 (1) through (3) of this subsection has been met. If the total number of units of housing required
5103 to be provided pursuant to paragraph (1) of this subsection has not been met, the amount of the
5104 real property tax exemption shall be reduced in equal proportion to the percentage of units of
5105 housing that are not currently operating in the given real property tax year.
5106 “(c) By December 31 of each tax year of the exemption period provided in subsection (b)
5107 of this section, the Mayor shall certify to the Office of Tax and Revenue what percentage of tax
5108 exemption the Property is eligible to receive under this section for that tax year. The Mayor shall
5109 notify the Office of Tax and Revenue if the Property ceases to be eligible for the exemption and
5110 the date such eligibility ceased.
5111 “(d) The exemptions provided by this section shall be in addition to, and not in lieu of,
5112 any other tax relief or assistance from any other source applicable to the Owner or Property.”.

5409 SUBTITLE S. REVISED REVENUE FUNDING
5410 Sec. 7261. Short title.
5411 This subtitle may be cited as the “Revised Revenue Funding Congressional Review
5412 Emergency Act of 2025”.
5413 Sec. 7262. (a) Notwithstanding any other provision of law, to the extent that Fiscal Year
5414 2025 local revenues certified in the September 2025 revenue estimate exceed the annual revenue
5415 estimate incorporated in the approved budget and financial plan for Fiscal Year 2025 and Fiscal
5416 Year 2025 revenues exceed actual expenditures as estimated by the Chief Financial Officer no
5417 later than November 15, 2025, these additional revenues shall be allocated and expended in
5418 Fiscal Year 2026 pursuant to the Appropriation of Additional Resources sections of the Fiscal
5419 Year 2026 Local Budget Act of 2025, passed on 2nd reading on July 28, 2025 (Enrolled version
5420 of Bill 26-260), and of the Fiscal Year 2026 Local Budget Emergency Act of 2025, passed on
5421 emergency basis on July 28, 2025 (Enrolled version of Bill 26-262), and pursuant to this section.
5422 (b) The additional revenues shall be allocated as follows:
292

5423 (1) The first $5,500,000 of one-time funds shall be allocated to the Office of the
5424 State Superintendent of Education to be spent on the Childcare Subsidy Program in Fiscal Year
5425 2026;
5426 (2) The next $1,500,000 of one-time funds shall be allocated to the Early
5427 Childhood Educator Pay Equity Fund at the Office of the State Superintendent in Fiscal Year
5428 2026;
5429 (3) The next $10,000,000 of one-time funds shall be allocated to the Housing
5430 Production Trust Fund to be spent on housing preservation in Fiscal Year 2026;
5431 (4) The next $3,500,000 of one-time funds shall be allocated to the Department of
5432 Forensic Sciences for in-house DNA testing in Fiscal Year 2026;
5433 (5) The next $500,000 of recurring funds shall be allocated to the Department of
5434 Healthcare Finance in each of Fiscal Years 2026, 2027, 2028, and 2029 to increase the Medicaid
5435 personal needs allowance;
5436 (6) The next $2,950,715 of one-time funds shall be allocated to the Department of
5437 Human Services to be spent on the Emergency Rental Assistance Program in Fiscal Year 2026;
5438 (7) The next $1,000,000 of one-time funds shall be allocated to the Department of
5439 Housing and Community Development to supplement its Housing Preservation Fund in Fiscal
5440 Year 2026;
293

5441 (8) The next $1,000,000 of one-time funds shall be allocated to the District of
5442 Columbia Public Charter School Board to be spent on lead-pipe testing in charter schools in
5443 Fiscal Year 2026;

5445 Amplified Sound Mitigation Regulation Amendment Act of 2024, effective March 21, 2025

5519 TITLE IX. APPLICABILITY; FISCAL IMPACT; EFFECTIVE DATE
5520 Sec. 9001. Applicability.
5521 Except as otherwise provided, this act shall apply as of October 1, 2025.
5522 Sec. 9002. Fiscal impact statement.
5523 The Council adopts the fiscal impact statement of the Chief Financial Officer as the fiscal
5524 impact statement required by section 4a of the General Legislative Procedures Act of 1975,
5525 approved October 16, 2006 (120 Stat. 2038; D.C. Official Code § 1-301.47a).
5526 Sec. 9003. Effective date.
5527 This act shall take effect following approval by the Mayor (or in the event of veto by the
5528 Mayor, action by the Council to override the veto), and shall remain in effect for no longer than
5529 90 days, as provided for emergency acts of the Council of the District of Columbia in section
5530 412(a) of the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 788;
5531 D.C. Official Code § 1-204.12(a)).
298
